# Chunked Encoding Stack Overflow
Chunked Encoding is one of the major methods by which RFC 7230 defines uploading and downloading of data. As Wikipedia puts it, a request (or response) body can be split up into parts with the chunked encoding transfer method as follows:
```
4\r\n        (bytes to send)
Wiki\r\n     (data)
6\r\n        (bytes to send)
pedia \r\n   (data)
E\r\n        (bytes to send)
in \r\n
\r\n
chunks.\r\n  (data)
0\r\n        (final byte - 0)
\r\n         (end message)
```
This, in layman's terms, means: "We will send 4 bytes; (sends 4 bytes); "we will send 6 bytes"; (sends 6 bytes); "we will send E" (in hexadecimal, and thus in decimal is 14) bytes; (sends 14 bytes); "We will send no data" ; connection ends (or possibly continues with a [pipelined request](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_pipelining).

An HTTP interpreter must be able to successfully parse the chunk lengths, and then subsequently parse the chunks of data, without knowing the total length of the final content. This is usually done with some sort of circular buffer.
## The Issue
Squid is able to successfully 'decode' chunked responses. It does this by buffering each chunk, and making space as each new chunk is sent. 

When a reply from the destination server is received, the function `HttpStateData::processReply` is called. From here, the reply headers are parsed. The reply body is finally parsed by calling `HttpStateData::processReplyBody`.

`HttpStateData::processReplyBody` performs some checks and actions to determine whether Squid should keep the connection open to receive more data. This is done using a switch:
```
        switch (persistentConnStatus()) {
        case INCOMPLETE_MSG: {
            debugs(11, 5, "processReplyBody: INCOMPLETE_MSG from " << serverConnection);
            /* Wait for more data or EOF condition */
            AsyncCall::Pointer nil;
            if (flags.keepalive_broken) {
                commSetConnTimeout(serverConnection, 10, nil);
            } else {
                commSetConnTimeout(serverConnection, Config.Timeout.read, nil);
            }

            flags.do_next_read = true;
        }
        break;
```
  Once this switch is broken from, the function finally calls ``HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody``, which always calls ``HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable``. The issue here is that ``HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable`` may once again call ``HttpStateData::processReply``, and the process will repeat.

It is therefore possible with a request to cause a stack overflow due to recursion. A backtrace from `gdb` further reveals the issue:
```
#5059 0x000000000105f520 in HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable (this=0x61300002cf98, doGrow=false) at http.cc:1633
#5060 0x0000000001071b00 in HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1603
#5061 0x00000000010711c1 in HttpStateData::processReplyBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1584
#5062 0x000000000104a006 in HttpStateData::processReply (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1330
#5063 0x000000000105f520 in HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable (this=0x61300002cf98, doGrow=false) at http.cc:1633
#5064 0x0000000001071b00 in HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1603
#5065 0x00000000010711c1 in HttpStateData::processReplyBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1584
#5066 0x000000000104a006 in HttpStateData::processReply (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1330
#5067 0x000000000105f520 in HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable (this=0x61300002cf98, doGrow=false) at http.cc:1633
#5068 0x0000000001071b00 in HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1603
#5069 0x00000000010711c1 in HttpStateData::processReplyBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1584
#5070 0x000000000104a006 in HttpStateData::processReply (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1330
#5071 0x000000000105f520 in HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable (this=0x61300002cf98, doGrow=false) at http.cc:1633
#5072 0x0000000001071b00 in HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1603
#5073 0x00000000010711c1 in HttpStateData::processReplyBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1584
#5074 0x000000000104a006 in HttpStateData::processReply (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1330
#5075 0x000000000105f520 in HttpStateData::maybeMakeSpaceAvailable (this=0x61300002cf98, doGrow=false) at http.cc:1633
#5076 0x0000000001071b00 in HttpStateData::maybeReadVirginBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1603
#5077 0x00000000010711c1 in HttpStateData::processReplyBody (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1584
#5078 0x000000000104a006 in HttpStateData::processReply (this=0x61300002cf98) at http.cc:1330
#5079 0x000000000105dc65 in HttpStateData::readReply (this=0x61300002cf98, io=...) at http.cc:1302
```
where frame #5079 is the initial reply read.

The following **base-64 encoded** response  is provided as a proof-of-concept. Simply decode it, and host it on a server which will keep the connection alive, for example, using `ncat`: `sudo ncat -l 80 -c 'cat decoded-file.txt' --keep-open`. You can then request the page using Squid as a proxy server, which will cause the stack overflow.
